  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_b3d6b3a3-cd20-4f36-b786-2116fc09a90f'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer6365823394801420530">THE PAST... Caught behind the lines of Hitler’s Final Solution, Saul Laski is one of the multitudes destined to die in the notorious Chelmno extermination camp.   <span id="freeText6365823394801420530" style="display:none">THE PAST... Caught behind the lines of Hitler’s Final Solution, Saul Laski is one of the multitudes destined to die in the notorious Chelmno extermination camp. Until he rises to meet his fate and finds himself face to face with an evil far older, and far greater, than the Nazi’s themselves...<br /><br />THE PRESENT... Compelled by the encounter to survive at all costs, so begins a journey that for Saul will span decades and cross continents, plunging into the darkest corners of 20th century history to reveal a secret society of beings who may often exist behind the world's most horrible and violent events. Killing from a distance, and by darkly manipulative proxy, they are people with the psychic ability to 'use' humans: read their minds, subjugate them to their wills, experience through their senses, feed off their emotions, force them to acts of unspeakable aggression. Each year, three of the most powerful of this hidden order meet to discuss their ongoing campaign of induced bloodshed and deliberate destruction. But this reunion, something will go terribly wrong. Saul’s quest is about to reach its elusive object, drawing hunter and hunted alike into a struggle that will plumb the depths of mankind’s attraction to violence, and determine the future of the world itself...</span>
  <a data-text-id="6365823394801420530" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span class='communityAnswererName'>

<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    It could happen! I wondered the same thing after reading that epilogue! But I think the reason the author left Melanie alive was to remind the reader <a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    It could happen! I wondered the same thing after reading that epilogue! But I think the reason the author left Melanie alive was to remind the reader that there's still monsters out there in the real world, and they still hold all the cards, existing for the sole purpose of causing humanity tremendous suffering. Melanie would have been extremely old since the epilogue was 7 years after Natalie burned her house down at the end of the book so hopefully she dies before she decides to use that submarine with the nukes she's controlling lol.<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>

<div id="review_2402810014" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2402810014" />
    <a title="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus"><img alt="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588320656p2/78485297.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2402810014?book_show_action=true">May 26, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " href="/user/show/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus">Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus?shelf=simmons-dan">simmons-dan</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2402810014" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2664164550013696730">Mind penetrating psi vampires haunt humankind in the same year Simmons´ ingenious sci-fi fantasy milestone Hyperion was published and revolutionize the horror genre in the same way. <br/><br/>King said that Simmons writes like a God and that he is a bit envious and what could exceed this quote? There is a handful of authors who unite the lucky combination of hard, lifelong perfecting their writing and talent and Simmons is in a league I find just some are coming close to. There may be authors just playing</span>
  <span id="freeText2664164550013696730" style="display:none">Mind penetrating psi vampires haunt humankind in the same year Simmons´ ingenious sci-fi fantasy milestone Hyperion was published and revolutionize the horror genre in the same way. <br /><br />King said that Simmons writes like a God and that he is a bit envious and what could exceed this quote? There is a handful of authors who unite the lucky combination of hard, lifelong perfecting their writing and talent and Simmons is in a league I find just some are coming close to. There may be authors just playing in one league that are as good or, regarding the worldbuilding but not characterization, better, but nobody writes works of such quality in different genres. Sci-Fi is totally my thing and I could name very few names of the same greatness as Hyperion, the same for horror and this one. <br /><br />It´s especially how it immediately blows one away, how it never gets boring for just a second, how it´s complexity is never confusing, the characters´ motivations logical, everything slowly escalating to amazing plot points,… And most of his novels are bricks, often with more than just 2 or 3 perspectives, time- and plotlines.<br /><br />There is often so less action, few cliffhangers, nothing one is used to in modern writing to pimp, accelerate, and distract from characterization, plotting, and logical flaws and errors, Simmons is using pure characterization and a complex, interwoven net of protagonists and antagonists to lead the long novel to a culmination of epic proportion. <br /><br />It´s a shame that I am too lazy to investigate which classic elements and tales inspired Simmons in and to his works, because his epic sci-fi novels are both filled with innuendos and connotations to famous ancient works or interpretations of these. Reader of the classics, mythologies, and history might find goldmines I am blind to see because of a lack of special knowledge.<br /><br />One of the cases where I absolutely don´t understand why people don´t like it. In other cases, there are elements that make it completely understandable that one can´t deal with too sciency, too charactery, too world buildy, too whatever elements, but this has everything, it´s the beginning of the career of one of the most talented and underrated writers of the 20th century. <br />So amazingly many pictures of this and Simmons´ other horror novel, Summer of night, that feels like a reinterpretation of Stephen Kings´ It, stay in mind, always a sure sign that the quality of the stuff is so high that it permanently blows ones´mind away and leaves one, wasted, but very happy, afterward.<br /><br />Tropes show how literature is conceptualized and created and which mixture of elements makes works and genres unique: <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Literature/CarrionComfort">https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.ph...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2664164550013696730" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_170648493" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/170648493" />
    <a title="Maciek" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2969647-maciek"><img alt="Maciek" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1280839159p2/2969647.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/170648493?book_show_action=true">May 24, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maciek" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maciek" href="/user/show/2969647-maciek">Maciek</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780312567071" href="/book/show/6631944-carrion-comfort">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">People with time</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Maciek by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/2445523-bondama">Bondama</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=own-in-paperback">own-in-paperback</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=friend-recommendations">friend-recommendations</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=owned-books">owned-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=big-tomes">big-tomes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer170648493" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7891449883464963060"><i>Carrion Comfort</i> is a beast of a book. My copy clocks in at 800 pages, and to be fair to mr. Simmons he kept the pace burning throughout the whole text. <br/><br/>There's much to enjoy in <i>Carrion Comfort</i>, and not the least of its good aspects is the premise. In this particular work Simmons tackles on one of the most famous horror creatures - the vampire. What makes it different from almost all other vampire ficton is his approach to the subject.<br/><br/><i>Carrion Comfort</i> is concerned with mind vampires, people who ca</span>
  <span id="freeText7891449883464963060" style="display:none"><i>Carrion Comfort</i> is a beast of a book. My copy clocks in at 800 pages, and to be fair to mr. Simmons he kept the pace burning throughout the whole text. <br /><br />There's much to enjoy in <i>Carrion Comfort</i>, and not the least of its good aspects is the premise. In this particular work Simmons tackles on one of the most famous horror creatures - the vampire. What makes it different from almost all other vampire ficton is his approach to the subject.<br /><br /><i>Carrion Comfort</i> is concerned with mind vampires, people who can enter the consciousness of any person and control their actions completely, like a puppeteer. Complete control, one from which there is no defense mental or physical, is certainly a frightening subject, and the opening set in 1942 Chelmno is pretty much stellar.<br /><br />The novel spans many years and locations, from WW2 Poland and surroundings to the 1980 USA. The WW2 pieces are seen in retrospect, and are certainly the best part of the novel; the obsession with chess that some characters have couldn't have been used in a better way. Simmons presents a scene that truly is horrifying and memorable in its intensity and eeriness.<br /><br />However, aside from the general premise and the few WW2 portions, <i>Carrion Comfort</i> is surprisingly short on the horror factor; most of the novel reads like a 80's thriller, complete with black helicopters, secret agents, explosives and multiple shoot outs, which occupy most of its pages. The characters are interesting (especially the elderly Melanie Fuller) but never fascinating, as they ought to be in a novel of such scope and ambition. The allusions to real people are certainly a nice touch, giving the novel some realism amidst all these bullets.<br /><br /><br />Overall, the books is compulsively readable, but rarely leaves anything unseen, and throughout its enormous lenght the reader will be exposed to as much action as he or she can take. The frenetic, Hollywood-like action can get a bit boring at times, and the true potential of the novel never really surfaces. Still, for such a huge tome it's a breezingly fast read, much more enjoyable that the plodding <i>Summer of Night</i>, although the book certainly did not need to be 800 pages long.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7891449883464963060" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText5938237130954978300" style="display:none">Spot on review. I am two thirds the way through the book and have found the same issues as you’ve discussed.<br /><br />It started promising, with a hint of intrigue, mind vampires being shadowy figures and metaphors of real life manipulation, and the possibility of developing fascinating characters. But having just finished a major (boring) action sequence with bulldozers etc. in German town, it has lost most the mystery that had me hooked at the start and become a very literal action flick with mind control. <br /><br />It’s as if Dan ran out of depth with the premise after the initial WWII story, and just went with making it a corny action flick.<br /><br />Curious of a good horror book you might recommend, given I think I liked and disliked similar things about this book :).</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/78065889" />
    <a title="Marvin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2160536-marvin"><img alt="Marvin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1485672728p2/2160536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/78065889?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marvin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marvin" href="/user/show/2160536-marvin">Marvin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780913165379" href="/book/show/924608.Carrion_Comfort">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2160536-marvin?shelf=autographed">autographed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2160536-marvin?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2160536-marvin?shelf=first-reads">first-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer78065889" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15039793457125356303">Exhibit C in "Authors Who Doodle"...<br/><br/><a href='http://tinypic.com?ref=fvxxra' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380329059i/691930.jpg' alt='Image and video hosting by TinyPic' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>In case you're interested, here's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/130241812' rel='nofollow noopener'>exhibit A</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/133715039' rel='nofollow noopener'>exhibit B</a>.<br/><br/><br/><i>Carrion Comfort</i>, Dan Simmons second novel, can be faulted for being overly long, needlessly complex and in dire need of a talented editor. Yet after I've said all that, it still remains one of the best horror novels of the second half of the 2oth century. The author has created a tense tale of mind control and the extremes of human corruption and power. While Simmons uses the term "Mind Vampires" fo</span>
  <span id="freeText15039793457125356303" style="display:none">Exhibit C in "Authors Who Doodle"...<br><br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=fvxxra" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380329059i/691930.jpg" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>In case you're interested, here's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/130241812" rel="nofollow noopener">exhibit A</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/133715039" rel="nofollow noopener">exhibit B</a>.<br><br><br><i>Carrion Comfort</i>, Dan Simmons second novel, can be faulted for being overly long, needlessly complex and in dire need of a talented editor. Yet after I've said all that, it still remains one of the best horror novels of the second half of the 2oth century. The author has created a tense tale of mind control and the extremes of human corruption and power. While Simmons uses the term "Mind Vampires" for his monsters, they are nothing like vampires and, at least in my mind, a hundred times more horrifying. The author's other strength in this 800 page novel is the development of strong protagonists and villains. These are not comic book characters but fully fleshed personalities with strong believable motivations. Simmons' setting starts in Auschwitz during World War II yet mainly takes place in the early 80s. Simmons sets a stage of believability by referencing a number of horrific events such as the Kennedy and Lennon assassinations and weaves a network of conspiracies and chess moves, the latter being a tantalizing motif throughout, that pulls this story way beyond the normal horror novel. If you must keep the vampire analogy, think of this as a cross between a vampire novel and "24" and you will get a hint of its themes. Any one who calls themselves a horror aficionado needs to read this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15039793457125356303" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13976389333419404607">This book! *covers eyes* oh my god! I don't know how to feel about it. Dan Simmons is such a great writer and his imagination scares me, like really, really bad! The stuff in this book was CRAZY! I couldn't believe what I was reading. Sometimes I didn't even want to know where this story was going. But despite the horrific plot, one thing that Simmons does really well is character building and backstory. Natalie and Saul are so fleshed out, they feel like real people and you are genuinely invest</span>
  <span id="freeText13976389333419404607" style="display:none">This book! *covers eyes* oh my god! I don't know how to feel about it. Dan Simmons is such a great writer and his imagination scares me, like really, really bad! The stuff in this book was CRAZY! I couldn't believe what I was reading. Sometimes I didn't even want to know where this story was going. But despite the horrific plot, one thing that Simmons does really well is character building and backstory. Natalie and Saul are so fleshed out, they feel like real people and you are genuinely invested in their lives which makes what happens to them so hard. <br />Especially Saul.<br />Saul might be one of my favorite protagonists in any story. A survivor against the most oppressive and terrifying odds. <br />Honorable mention is Rob Gentry. I love Rob. A true hero. But this story would be nothing without the anti heroes-the enemies-the villains. No other villains in any other book are as merciless, self serving, cruel or disgusting than the soul sucking Users inCarrion Comfort. I enjoyed most of it but sometimes, I admit, it went too far. So I docked it a whole star for just being too damn long (I could have shaved off at least a couple hundred pages EASILY) and for some unnecessary roughness. Mainly I got tired of my sensitivities being offended which probably wouldn't have happened if this were a shorter book. Anyhow, four stars is still four stars and a worthy horror novel. I'm glad it's over. Hahah</span>

<div id="review_571312845" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/571312845" />
    <a title="Bradley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley"><img alt="Bradley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508811508p2/4213258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/571312845?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bradley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bradley" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley">Bradley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=2016-shelf">2016-shelf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer571312845" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4048954229263235766">So I'm changing my final score on this novel from a solid 3 to a generous 4 stars, because the book was JUST THAT UNPREDICTABLE.<br/><br/>That's an odd thing to say as a re-read, no?<br/><br/>There's lots of places where the novel easily deserves a 5 star, just on reflection, alone, and since this came out nearly 30 years ago I'm not going to fuss too much over spoilers. <br/><br/>Do You Like Chess?<br/><br/>Then this novel is for you.<br/><br/>Do you like mind-vampires that look, feel, and act like Donald Trump, Conservative Religious Nutsos, </span>
  <span id="freeText4048954229263235766" style="display:none">So I'm changing my final score on this novel from a solid 3 to a generous 4 stars, because the book was JUST THAT UNPREDICTABLE.<br /><br />That's an odd thing to say as a re-read, no?<br /><br />There's lots of places where the novel easily deserves a 5 star, just on reflection, alone, and since this came out nearly 30 years ago I'm not going to fuss too much over spoilers. <br /><br />Do You Like Chess?<br /><br />Then this novel is for you.<br /><br />Do you like mind-vampires that look, feel, and act like Donald Trump, Conservative Religious Nutsos, Concentration Camp Masters, or quiet, unassuming matrons who take on entire inner-city gangs? <br /><br />Then this novel is for you.<br /><br />Do you also like long and rambling adventures populated by normal folk caught up in the nightmare of marionettes, either trying to escape the nightmare or get revenge for the things that had been done to them? As in Full-Blown Epic-Length rambling and character-development-through-action for almost 900 pages, with a nearly uncountable number of reversals, sad deaths, and improbable successes?<br /><br />Then this novel is for you.<br /><br />Honestly, I never had any issues with anything in particular. This was a pretty epic horror novel filled with tons of mind-jumping, mind and body controlling, and history. The focus on the details is what made it pretty damn awesome, but that's what horror is all about. <br /><br />If I were to put my issue into words, I'd still have a hard time, because its faults were also its strengths. It was unpredictable. <br /><br />I can't say I liked most of the characters, and it was really hard to actually enjoy being in the minds of the baddies, but Melanie was a real treat. Saul, more than anyone, was complex and multifaceted and sits in my mind, as back when I first read this when it was new, as the quintessential portrait of a nazi-hunter/vampire-hunter. Hell, I've been judging all other novels with the trope by this gold standard ever since.<br /><br />I'm glad I re-read this, but my god it was long. There was so much, by my older and jaded eyes, that I think could have been cut right the hell out, but it was a horror novel first and foremost, and having a long build-up before the missiles come and destroy the island (or whatever) is still what we seek in the style. <br /><br />If you want a very long and interesting ride, a near perfect diversion with lots of sex, horror, and a cast of baddies with zero moral fortitude and the undercurrent that they *might* get what's coming to them, then I really recommend this novel. :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="4048954229263235766" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1299841616" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1299841616" />
    <a title="Edward Lorn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn"><img alt="Edward Lorn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492199506p2/8850418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1299841616?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Edward Lorn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Edward Lorn" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn">Edward Lorn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">not many people</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1299841616" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14575105253616120702">I always hesitate to say a book is overlong. I read because I like knowing the deepest thoughts and motivations of the characters who populate my fiction. Books are meant to be longer, more in-depth experiences. There are thousands of studies that have been done on chapter and novel length, but the truth of the matter is: a reader only notices page count when the writing and/or story sucks. <br/><br/>I find myself questioning whether or not I think a book is going on too long, I ask: Was I ever bored for </span>
  <span id="freeText14575105253616120702" style="display:none">I always hesitate to say a book is overlong. I read because I like knowing the deepest thoughts and motivations of the characters who populate my fiction. Books are meant to be longer, more in-depth experiences. There are thousands of studies that have been done on chapter and novel length, but the truth of the matter is: a reader only notices page count when the writing and/or story sucks. <br /><br />I find myself questioning whether or not I think a book is going on too long, I ask: Was I ever bored for extended periods of time? You can have a long book with lulls, but the action should kick back in right around the time your average reader will start skimming. (In a perfect world, a reader will never feel like skimming, but we all know that even the best novels can have unneeded information) This, in the realm of fiction, is called pacing. It is my opinion (mind you this opinion is based solely on this book, as I have not read anything else by Dan Simmons, but <i>Carrion Comfort</i> is the novel that put him on the map, so I'm judging it as a good example of his work) that Dan Simmons is crap at pacing, and he is absolutely in love with his own voice. <br /><br />For a novel of 884 pages (and teensy-tiny type to boot, at least in my paperback copy), I found only three memorable scenes. The opening, the final fight with the "Honky Monster", (who we will discuss more in a minute) and the final fight with Justin. Everything else was either <i>meh</i> or downright boring. I feel comfortable saying this book is way too long based on the content received. I could have done without 50% of this book. And no, that's no exaggeration.<br /><br />A great bit of my enjoyment factor was hindered by the repetition of the word "Negress". Listen, I understand that Negroe used to be an acceptable word. Likewise, I get that Black was once a racial slur. I get it. I'm not talking about that. I simply do not like the sound of the word "Negress". I feel about this word the same way some people feel about "cunt" or "twat". The word just sounds ugly, and I don't want to listen to it. Doesn't matter what it means or if it was ever acceptable. If the word was a person, it would have a punchable face. Unfortunately, I switched to the audiobook at around the halfway mark so I literally had to listen to this woman say the word dozens of times. And no, that is no exaggeration either. Yes, this book is dated, but even if I went back in time to when this book was released in 1989, I still can't imagine the necessity for such word repetition. Seems like lazy writing to me. I mean, at one point, the word is used as much as "she" and "her". <br /><br />Another huge letdown was the lack of horror. The cover promised "EPIC HORROR" and other checks the book's ass couldn't cash. There were horror tropes, sure, but there was very little that was horrifying. <i>Carrion Comfort</i> is the same kind of horror experience you'd receive if you watched a marathon of the <i>Underworld</i> films. This is action-horror, and I don't like action-horror. Yeah, there are monsters, but they aren't scary. They are rapey and over-the-top, but they aren't frightening. The one truly terrifying monster in the book is figuratively castrated by the fact that the author thought it would be a sound idea to call him the "Honky Monster". Sweet baby Tom Cruise, I wish to fuck I was kidding. This scythe-wielding baddie is turned into a joke shortly after his introduction, and he never reclaims his rightful spot as scary. Every time he was named, I laughed. Out loud. I literally barked laughter. Such a well-designed monster should not garner guffaws based on his moniker alone. I don't know what I would have called him, but it sure as shit wouldn't have been "Honky Monster". This is the equivalent of naming Dracula the "Neck Sucker!" Get the fuck outta here!<br /><br />Oh, and I'm not a chess player. I feel that I missed a great deal of subtext because I do not play the game. And that sucks. This book did, however, make me pick up a book about chess, and I'm enjoying learning how to play, but I know I have many miles to go and I wasn't about to put off finishing this book while I boned up on my middle game.<br /><br />A final note on the writing. Dan Simmons doesn't write like a modern author. His prose is elegant and Dickensian. I was not expecting that. While it shouldn't have been so jarring, it most certainly was. I can dig good writing no matter the style, but I don't think it fit this subject matter. It was horribly awkward in places. Imagine Shakespeare writing <i>The Grapes of Wrath</i> or <i>Of Mice and Men</i>. That would be weird, right? Now imagine Charles Dickens wrote a horror-thriller in the vein of early Dean Koontz. I think you see my issue.<br /><br />In summation: I'm not giving up on Simmons. I want to see what he does with some historical fiction. I have <i>Drood</i> and <i>The Terror</i> queued up in the next few months. Both novels are equally long , so if I don't like them I'll probably quit Simmons after that. I love the concept of <i>Drood</i> and probably should have started there.<br /><br /><b>Final Judgment: Needs Jazzercize! and Slim Fast.</b><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14575105253616120702" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13294707064331064973">Just finished reading Carrion Comfort (again), 30 years after first discovering this incredible work by Dan Simmons. After all this time, this classic horror tale is still as impactful as it was when I was just a young 22-year-old Marine, and this read just reaffirms its place as my second-favorite novel of all time. Carrion Comfort was, is, and always shall be a confirmed ⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐ read.</span>

<div id="review_1399172747" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1399172747" />
    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23841736-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532221628p2/23841736.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1399172747?book_show_action=true">Sep 23, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/23841736-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">People who like horror and suspense</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23841736-sarah?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23841736-sarah?shelf=world-fantasy-nominee">world-fantasy-nominee</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1399172747" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6554950877400654602">Five words that I never thought I would say: "Couldn't it have been longer?". Seriously, for someone who dreads a book that passes the 600 page mark, I should have been absolutely dying over this 900 page monster. But...<br/><br/>This is one of those rare horror books that manages to maintain the suspense and horror over the course of the book. Long books often make it difficult for the author to maintain suspense without the story dragging (I'm totally looking at you Stephen King) but I found that Simmon</span>
  <span id="freeText6554950877400654602" style="display:none">Five words that I never thought I would say: "Couldn't it have been longer?". Seriously, for someone who dreads a book that passes the 600 page mark, I should have been absolutely dying over this 900 page monster. But...<br /><br />This is one of those rare horror books that manages to maintain the suspense and horror over the course of the book. Long books often make it difficult for the author to maintain suspense without the story dragging (I'm totally looking at you Stephen King) but I found that Simmons managed to maintain a fairly consistent level of suspense. In 884 pages and 39:32 of audio, I was never once bored. Another truly impressive thing was that he created some of the most harrowing scenes I've ever read in a horror book but he never relied on gore to do it. Chess? Yes, I will never look at chess the same way again.<br /><br />Much of the suspense of the story is in how it develops so I don't want to give a synopsis. I'll just say that there are these really bad dudes (and dudettes) that are able to control the actions of other people. Over the course of the book they're eventually called "mind vampires". One of the bad guys does use this for sexual violence so there are definitely triggers in this, but it did only happen at the beginning and then the story became much larger and more complex and he wasn't in the book enough for it to be a consistent issue.<br /><br />A horror book with only one disemboweling and characters that redefine sadism. It was a very solid 4 stars and easily pushing 4.5. A truly fantastic book and now I want to read anything Simmons has written.<br /><br />EDIT: I'm increasing the rating to 5 stars. I'm comparing it to all of my monthly reads and I have several 5 star reads, yet this was my favorite read of all of them.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6554950877400654602" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_98632118" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/98632118" />
    <a title="mark monday" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/131922-mark-monday"><img alt="mark monday" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572672245p2/131922.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/98632118?book_show_action=true">Apr 15, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="mark monday" class="user" itemprop="url" name="mark monday" href="/user/show/131922-mark-monday">mark monday</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/131922-mark-monday?shelf=horror-60s-70s-80s">horror-60s-70s-80s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/131922-mark-monday?shelf=blood-and-danger">blood-and-danger</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer98632118" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2099030942304448116">this is a briskly-paced supernatural thriller about mind control and controlling the world around us. it is also about as one-dimensional as they come, despite the potential of the multi-leveled subject matter and the breadth of the narrative (from World War 2 Germany to present-day Hollywood, and dozens of locales in between). the novel and several of the characters are obsessed with chess, which makes for some intriguing action. although it includes several wonderfully creepy set-pieces, overa</span>
  <span id="freeText2099030942304448116" style="display:none">this is a briskly-paced supernatural thriller about mind control and controlling the world around us. it is also about as one-dimensional as they come, despite the potential of the multi-leveled subject matter and the breadth of the narrative (from World War 2 Germany to present-day Hollywood, and dozens of locales in between). the novel and several of the characters are obsessed with chess, which makes for some intriguing action. although it includes several wonderfully creepy set-pieces, overall this is far more action-oriented than horror. this is Simmons' second book, which must be the explanation for the occasionally stilted writing and the clear need of an editor. <br /><br />the single first-person strand amongst all the third-person narratives is from one of the villainous 'mind vampires', which allows for some enjoyably tricky twists of perspective during various loaded scenes. and it certainly helps to create a devious and punchy ending. besides being an intriguing tool for the narrative, i think that this character is the novel's chief strength: a very ironic portrait of a vicious, racist, murderous, insanely self-absorbed, semi-senile southern belle - but one who also manages to be somewhat sympathetic and surprisingly funny. particularly when detailing her prudish and judgmental view of modern society. what a bitch! but not just any bitch - a mind-controlling bitch who will get you and all of your loved ones if you stand in her way! just imagine if prudish, semi-senile southern belles were in control of your mind and body...<i>shudder</i>. the things they'd do!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2099030942304448116" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_460367268" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/460367268" />
    <a title="Adam Light" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7004622-adam-light"><img alt="Adam Light" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481355960p2/7004622.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/460367268?book_show_action=true">Nov 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Adam Light" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Adam Light" href="/user/show/7004622-adam-light">Adam Light</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7004622-adam-light?shelf=paperback">paperback</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7004622-adam-light?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7004622-adam-light?shelf=own-it">own-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7004622-adam-light?shelf=my-personal-favorites">my-personal-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7004622-adam-light?shelf=dan-simmons">dan-simmons</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer460367268" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17304247267270637915">I like long books, and Carrion Comfort is very long. Clocking in at 886 pages, it isn't the longest I have read, either. The tiny typeface may have shortened the page count, though. I would love to find out the word count of this book. <br/>I say all this not to criticize the book (as you can see, I rated it 5 stars) but to explain why it took forever to read it.<br/>I almost dropped a star because there is some extraneous material here that could have been excised and the mind-blowing story would not hav</span>
  <span id="freeText17304247267270637915" style="display:none">I like long books, and Carrion Comfort is very long. Clocking in at 886 pages, it isn't the longest I have read, either. The tiny typeface may have shortened the page count, though. I would love to find out the word count of this book. <br />I say all this not to criticize the book (as you can see, I rated it 5 stars) but to explain why it took forever to read it.<br />I almost dropped a star because there is some extraneous material here that could have been excised and the mind-blowing story would not have suffered, but I savored every one of the words, so I feel that would be wrong.<br />This was my first Dan Simmons book and I had no real idea what to expect. I did know from friends warning me, to ignore the cover blurb comparing this to King's The Stand, so I was not disappointed to find the two are worlds apart, but both are epic in scope and flawlessly executed.<br />I don't remember who first recommended this book to me, but thanks a lot whoever you are.<br />I was lost in this story as soon as I opened it. The horror is not in your face here, but takes a backseat to more action and suspense than I expected. You get monsters, but they are not what you expect at all, at least that is how I feel.<br />The antagonists, and there are too many to count, are some of the most sadistic, vile and racist bunch I have encountered. I can' t help but compare the True Knot from Doctor Sleep to this group, only severely watered down and nowhere near as creepy. Maybe it is due to having read King's newest while I read this one. Not sure, but there are similarities.<br />I could go on forever but I finished this at 3 am and I have to stop.<br />I don't want to spoil anything but I will say that Saul was my favorite character. He was so well written, I never doubted his authenticity one bit. Rob Gentry and Natalie Preston were equally good.<br />As I mentioned, the bad guys are EVIL, and we even get a first person account from one of them, while the rest is told in third. That was interesting, and Melanie's scenes damn near steal the book.<br />This one gets a big well deseved 5 from me.<br />I will be reading more Simmons for sure.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17304247267270637915" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_350071340" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/350071340" />
    <a title="Kathryn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6504379-kathryn"><img alt="Kathryn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590065910p2/6504379.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/350071340?book_show_action=true">Jun 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathryn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathryn" href="/user/show/6504379-kathryn">Kathryn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6504379-kathryn?shelf=horror-read">horror-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6504379-kathryn?shelf=2012-read">2012-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6504379-kathryn?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer350071340" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7154416445207407774"><i>Carrion Comfort</i> is a mess of a book. Not only are there evil, mind-controlling vampires, the things they do are just so ripe with evil. It's almost like they give evil a new name. <br/><br/><i>Carrion Comfort</i>'s story is complex, and involves several parties. Not only are these parties involved in a bigger picture, but they also have their own stories and action. There really isn't a main character, but several main characters, and several minor characters. As far as main characters go, Saul was my definite f</span>
  <span id="freeText7154416445207407774" style="display:none"><i>Carrion Comfort</i> is a mess of a book. Not only are there evil, mind-controlling vampires, the things they do are just so ripe with evil. It's almost like they give evil a new name. <br /><br /><i>Carrion Comfort</i>'s story is complex, and involves several parties. Not only are these parties involved in a bigger picture, but they also have their own stories and action. There really isn't a main character, but several main characters, and several minor characters. As far as main characters go, Saul was my definite favorite. His story from the past to the present was so intriguing, and his time in WWII in the concentration camps was probably my favorite part of the entire novel. His cat and mouse relationship with the one and only Oberst was interesting, and I found myself cheering for him to succeed and avenge what and who the Oberst had done and is. The other characters: Natalie, Rob, Melanie, and Harod were also some of my favorite characters. Even though some of those characters were part of the evil side, I found I still enjoyed reading about them. <br /><br />When it comes Melanie, I have to say...what an evil bitch. I'm sorry if that offends you, but if you read this novel, you would know why I say that. To Use, and I capitalize "U" for a reason, people the way she did, ugh.....That is all I will say. She was entertaining, and I felt like I could hear her voice in my head when her story was being read. <br /><br />Harod.....I have nothing nice to say about that @*($#(#$. I'm not kidding. If you've read the book, you know EXACTLY what I am talking about. SICK PERVERT. The airplane and the hot tub scenes, along with what he did to Natalie...<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[He deserved what he got in the end. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I did find his story entertaining, to say the very least. <br /><br />Everyone's character was perfect for <i>Carrion Comfort</i>. The story is very well done, but there were a few problems I had with it. <br /><br />First, I think some of this book could have been cut out. There was a point where I felt like I was going to gouge my eyes out at one point because I kept feeling like the story just kept going, and going, and going.....But whatever...The overall story is NOT disappointing, and has LOTS of action. <br /><br />Second, I didn't find this book scary at all. Disturbing, yes...but not scary. I was expecting something scary, I guess. It didn't disappoint, but I guess it was just the expectation which kind of made it a little bit of a problem for me. <br /><br />Third, there were a few instances where I was wondering, "How did we get there from where we were?" It kind of felt like an action was missing...That's kind of a minor thing. I'm a very visual reader, and this book is very visual.<br /><br />Finally, there was a very, VERY memorable scene for me. Something I don't think I'll ever forget...<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The WWII chess game where Saul is introduced to the Oberst. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> It was such a surreal scene, and like I said, it is one I won't soon forget. The impact the scene has on the entire novel, and how it lets you know how much evil people can be fraught with, was just astounding. <br /><br />For most of the book, I'd say two-thirds of the way, it was a five star book. But, I've gotten to be a bit more critical lately, a little bit more honest, and the few minor things I had knocked it down to a four star. I haven't decided whether I'm going to keep this book or not. I usually keep the books which are my favorites and can't part with. I think the hidden scene I mentioned before is enough for me to keep it, and along with Saul's background story. Very intriguing, and for me the best parts of the book. <br /><br /><i>Carrion Comfort</i> is definitely worth the read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7154416445207407774" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText5947458724635223501" style="display:none">One glance of the wear on the spine of my copy of Carrion Comfort would be enough to tell this is a must read. In fact, I would upload a picture of it but yet another of my friends is currently reading it. One of my friends read it three times and another wants it back again.<br />It's a toss-up between this novel and Silence of the Lambs as my favorite novel of all time.<br />It's huge, over 900 pages, and dates back from Nazi Germany to present day. In a nutshell, it's about a small group of people with the ability to completely control the actions of people using telekinesis. For those who have read the novel, this little tidbit will interest you:<br />I saw an interview with Dan Simmons...the inspiration for this story came from a dream he had of an old woman in a nightgown being pursued through a forest by a helicopter.<br />Amazing how this story grew from that. I can't recommend this highly enough. Read it!!</span>

<div id="review_1851561248" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1851561248" />
    <a title="Ashley Daviau" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35915119-ashley-daviau"><img alt="Ashley Daviau" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599784716p2/35915119.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1851561248?book_show_action=true">Aug 02, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley Daviau" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley Daviau" href="/user/show/35915119-ashley-daviau">Ashley Daviau</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780312567071" href="/book/show/6631944-carrion-comfort">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1851561248" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10972110425305408200">I’m kind of torn in two when it comes to this book. I was seriously disappointed by it but at the same time, I did really enjoy some parts. I think my disappointment stems from the fact that I’ve read over and over how scary this book is and I didn’t even find myself remotely scared. Sure some parts were pretty brutal and the actions of many characters were truly despicable but I just didn’t feel any fear when reading this. Nothing about this book made me want to sleep with the lights on at nigh</span>
  <span id="freeText10972110425305408200" style="display:none">I’m kind of torn in two when it comes to this book. I was seriously disappointed by it but at the same time, I did really enjoy some parts. I think my disappointment stems from the fact that I’ve read over and over how scary this book is and I didn’t even find myself remotely scared. Sure some parts were pretty brutal and the actions of many characters were truly despicable but I just didn’t feel any fear when reading this. Nothing about this book made me want to sleep with the lights on at night and that’s what I love about reading horror, the adrenaline that the fright brings. The story was interesting though and I enjoyed how everything was so intertwined, Simmons really spun a tangled web and it kept me intrigued enough to see it through to the end. I did think the ending was great, and gave me tingles, I wish the whole book would have felt that way! </span>
  <a data-text-id="10972110425305408200" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1752315813" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1752315813" />
    <a title="Johann (jobis89)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50893023-johann-jobis89"><img alt="Johann (jobis89)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588540681p2/50893023.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1752315813?book_show_action=true">Dec 23, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Johann (jobis89)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Johann (jobis89)" href="/user/show/50893023-johann-jobis89">Johann (jobis89)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780312567071" href="/book/show/6631944-carrion-comfort">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1752315813" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14230307296383095541">"If everyone could understand the working of a psychopath's mind, we undoubtedly would be closer to insanity ourselves."<br/><br/>Carrion Comfort focuses on a small group of the population who possess what they call the "Ability", which is the power to take over someone's mind and completely control them, and even prompt them to commit murder. It is proposed that this Ability has been present for years, with reference to the Holocaust as well as random murders of individuals. A small group come together w</span>
  <span id="freeText14230307296383095541" style="display:none">"If everyone could understand the working of a psychopath's mind, we undoubtedly would be closer to insanity ourselves."<br /><br />Carrion Comfort focuses on a small group of the population who possess what they call the "Ability", which is the power to take over someone's mind and completely control them, and even prompt them to commit murder. It is proposed that this Ability has been present for years, with reference to the Holocaust as well as random murders of individuals. A small group come together with the intention of stopping a small group responsible for these awful actions.<br /><br />First of all, this book is absolutely mammoth. My edition was nearly 800 pages with a teeny tiny font...I'm no stranger to big books, I am a King fan after all, but this one felt particularly long. Possibly because the story was so heavy and depressing at times, with no comedic relief or light moments! Nevertheless, it was a great book, intricately planned with awesome characters. Saul, Natalie and Rob Gentry were all solid protagonists, and likeable! Compare these to the "mind vampires" in the novel and there is no competition. The mind vampires are disgusting, vile, horrible, evil people. I've never encountered such hateful characters in all my reading days. Nothing redeemable about any of them!<br /><br />The book itself was terrifying in parts. Some creepy, tense moments and horrifying characters. The premise that these individuals could control your mind and actions from a distance away is just...terrifying. That you could be used to commit someone else's horrible deeds is scary indeed. One compliment is also that this book is very unpredictable...I never saw anything coming, it keep surprising me over and over.<br /><br />A complaint would be that the book did feel too long...did Simmons not hire an editor? This doesn't take away from the enjoyment of the book, but it could have done with some serious editing. I especially don't really enjoy "action" scenes where people are just running around for ages and hiding in different locations - this kind of thing is great for the big screen, but can be hard to follow when reading.<br /><br />It's a complicated book to rate because some parts were 5 stars and some parts felt more like 3 stars...therefore I think an average of 4 stars is best! Highly recommend, but don't read if easily offended or if you're not a fan of gore and violence.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14230307296383095541" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8414616828606499036">Hyperion gets a lot of love but I seldom see any mention of this amazing book. It is very different from Hyperion but that is not unusual for Simmons as he is a very versatile writer. Carrion Comfort is sf/horror of the highest calibre, something Stephen King may write when he is on top form (but with better prose). This book is about people with mind control abilities of different strengths. A lot of riveting plot is generated from this simple premise. I won't go onto any details, I'll just rec</span>
  <span id="freeText8414616828606499036" style="display:none">Hyperion gets a lot of love but I seldom see any mention of this amazing book. It is very different from Hyperion but that is not unusual for Simmons as he is a very versatile writer. Carrion Comfort is sf/horror of the highest calibre, something Stephen King may write when he is on top form (but with better prose). This book is about people with mind control abilities of different strengths. A lot of riveting plot is generated from this simple premise. I won't go onto any details, I'll just recommend that you do not miss this book even if you don't normally read horror.</span>

<div id="review_1835063495" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1835063495" />
    <a title="Abbie | ab_reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53055819-abbie-ab-reads"><img alt="Abbie | ab_reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545340790p2/53055819.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1835063495?book_show_action=true">Dec 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Abbie | ab_reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Abbie | ab_reads" href="/user/show/53055819-abbie-ab-reads">Abbie | ab_reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780747234050" href="/book/show/924610.Carrion_Comfort">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1835063495" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3469468398467467047">This book should come with a warning label, although that might ruin its amazing cover. Dan Simmons has managed to bring together literally every single horrible thing you could think of - the holocaust, sexual abuse, racism, corruption, torture - and smush it all together in one giant volume that you keep reading in spite of yourself. It clocks in at just under 1000 pages and I read it in 4 days. I'm now on my way to church to cleanse myself.<br/>.<br/>Carrion Comfort boasts some of the most despicable c</span>
  <span id="freeText3469468398467467047" style="display:none">This book should come with a warning label, although that might ruin its amazing cover. Dan Simmons has managed to bring together literally every single horrible thing you could think of - the holocaust, sexual abuse, racism, corruption, torture - and smush it all together in one giant volume that you keep reading in spite of yourself. It clocks in at just under 1000 pages and I read it in 4 days. I'm now on my way to church to cleanse myself.<br />.<br />Carrion Comfort boasts some of the most despicable characters I've ever had the displeasure of coming across. Melanie Fuller, a racist old lady, William Borden, an ex-Nazi, Tony Harod, a rapist in an unfortunate position of power in Hollywood... Oh and they all have the power of mind control. Mind vampires, as Simmons terms them.<br />.<br />To balance the legit most awful bad guys ever, Simmons gives us Natalie Preston, Saul Laski, and Rob Gentry (although sometimes my edition kept putting 'Ron Gentry, how annoying). Having seen and experienced their evil firsthand, our trio bands together to fight it.<br />.<br />I loved this book, as sick as it is. It's heart-breaking, raw, powerful, stomach-turning, violent, gory, just absolutely mad. I gave it 4 stars because it could definitely have been edited down (I don't need to read about people chasing after rogue cherry tomatoes with their forks while eating a salad), I was exhausted after a 150-200 page epic fight/showdown in the middle, and the constant racial and sexual slurs did wear me down. I fucking loved the ending though, was not expecting that!<br />.<br />Horror lovers, read it, but I reiterate, not for the fainthearted! Oh also, some knowledge of chess might enhance your reading experience!<br />.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3469468398467467047" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6810645-sheila?shelf=vintage-horror">vintage-horror</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer286236044" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4987642194411620424">1 star--I didn't like it. Wrong reader!<br/><br/>Dan Simmons, the author of this book, also wrote Hyperion, which I adore. So I was disappointed that this book wasn't to my taste. First, I expected (and wanted) horror, and instead, this is more of a blockbuster thriller--lots of FBI agents and explosions and such. <br/><br/>Second, I was turned off by the graphic rape scenes. They were done by a "bad guy" and not presented as anything positive, but I could do without the descriptions of a woman's fear and pain--esp</span>
  <span id="freeText4987642194411620424" style="display:none">1 star--I didn't like it. Wrong reader!<br /><br />Dan Simmons, the author of this book, also wrote Hyperion, which I adore. So I was disappointed that this book wasn't to my taste. First, I expected (and wanted) horror, and instead, this is more of a blockbuster thriller--lots of FBI agents and explosions and such. <br /><br />Second, I was turned off by the graphic rape scenes. They were done by a "bad guy" and not presented as anything positive, but I could do without the descriptions of a woman's fear and pain--especially when it happened more than once in the book and didn't move the plot along. (We get it--he's a rapist.)<br /><br />And on a similar note, I was tired of reading the n-word and other racial slurs. Again, done by the bad guys, but I found it wearying.<br /><br />I wish there had been more mental vampirism and less racism! All in all, not for me, though I know a lot of people who love this book so YMMV.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4987642194411620424" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1855467711" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16920116328168336829">DNF -<br/><br/>This book for me is abit of a mess, my first Dan Simmons came in as The Terror which was a phenomenal horror story that got recommended to me here on Goodreads and I adored it. The style, atmosphere and characters created one amazing horror. Carrion Comfort did not however do this for me.<br/><br/>Carrion Comfort is about a group of beings that can control people to do anything and they can of feed off the life force of those effected by it. Its sort of a free take on vampires turning the victims int</span>
  <span id="freeText16920116328168336829" style="display:none">DNF -<br /><br />This book for me is abit of a mess, my first Dan Simmons came in as The Terror which was a phenomenal horror story that got recommended to me here on Goodreads and I adored it. The style, atmosphere and characters created one amazing horror. Carrion Comfort did not however do this for me.<br /><br />Carrion Comfort is about a group of beings that can control people to do anything and they can of feed off the life force of those effected by it. Its sort of a free take on vampires turning the victims into Thralls. Now the premise is very good and it does start really strong but I found that about a 3rd of the way through it started to get a little lost in itself.<br /><br />Characters didn't seem to be consistent Melanie for example has a massive character change from being opposed to what she was doing to now being evil about her use with it. The amazing horror slasher scene that happens early in the book also is brilliant however future scenes seem alittle forced and just not interesting or maybe its just that the first scene was just so unexpected but it made all future 'horror' just dull.<br /><br />I also found this book a hard read due to the derogatory comments about well everyone it didnt make it a nice read plus alot of horrific things happen that are just shocking such as forced incest and child murder.<br /><br />The book just became too run of the mill for me and wasnt too my taste. Dan Simmons is still a great writer though.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16920116328168336829" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer31543589" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13755118256269902266">The print of this large paperback is so small, I imagine that if it were in hardback, I wouldn't be able to pick it up and read it. I think this book, while a good read with some fantastic, scary parts in it, could have used a tad more editing. <br/><br/>I must say that some of the characters are truly monstrous. Tony, the producer, is a vile human being. The arrogant movers and shakers in the secret society couldn't have less empathy for their fellow human beings. But no one, not even Willi IMO, comes cl</span>
  <span id="freeText13755118256269902266" style="display:none">The print of this large paperback is so small, I imagine that if it were in hardback, I wouldn't be able to pick it up and read it. I think this book, while a good read with some fantastic, scary parts in it, could have used a tad more editing. <br /><br />I must say that some of the characters are truly monstrous. Tony, the producer, is a vile human being. The arrogant movers and shakers in the secret society couldn't have less empathy for their fellow human beings. But no one, not even Willi IMO, comes close to the monstrosity of the old lady Melanie. The ease at which she ruins lives and Uses people is unsettling. Even when she could leave it alone, she will still go back and exact revenge on anyone who dares stop her detailed plans to get what she wants when she wants it. <br /><br />The most chilling scenes for me were of Willi's younger years as a Nazi, and his dabbles into the lives of concentration camp prisoners. That human chess game was horrifying.<br /><br />This is a book I had heard about many times and I'm glad I finally read it.</span>

          </span>
        </div>
